        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The status of ambient temp. sodium ion batteries is reviewed in light of recent developments in anode, electrolyte and cathode materials.  These devices, although early in their stage of development, are promising for large-scale grid storage applications due to the abundance and very low cost of sodium-contg. precursors used to make the components.  The engineering knowledge developed recently for highly successful Li ion batteries can be leveraged to ensure rapid progress in this area, although different electrode materials and electrolytes will be required for dual intercalation systems based on sodium.  In particular, new anode materials need to be identified, since the graphite anode, commonly used in lithium systems, does not intercalate sodium to any appreciable extent.  A wider array of choices is available for cathodes, including high performance layered transition metal oxides and polyanionic compds.  Recent developments in electrodes are encouraging, but a great deal of research is necessary, particularly in new electrolytes, and the understanding of the SEI films.  The engineering modeling calcns. of Na-ion battery energy d. indicate that 210 Wh kg-1 in gravimetric energy is possible for Na-ion batteries compared to existing Li-ion technol. if a cathode capacity of 200 mAh g-1 and a 500 mAh g-1 anode can be discovered with an av. cell potential of 3.3 V.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGojsFXLPEQzILVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liXuxKzYCdXIQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XntlSnurc%253D&amp;md5=fa5d7d089d261a40896cb6b03e88bfbe</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref3'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit3" data-doi="10.1039/c3ee40847g"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Pan, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, Y.-S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, L.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Room-temperature stationary sodium-ion batteries for large-scale electric energy storage</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Energy Environ.                         cas_cit3R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">3</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Room-temperature stationary sodium-ion batteries for large-scale electric energy storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Pan, Huilin; Hu, Yong-Sheng; Chen, Liquan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">8</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2338-2360</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EESNBY</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1754-5706</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Room-temp. stationary sodium-ion batteries have attracted great attention particularly in large-scale elec. energy storage applications for renewable energy and smart grid because of the huge abundant sodium resources and low cost.  In this article, a variety of electrode materials including cathodes and anodes as well as electrolytes for room-temp. stationary sodium-ion batteries are briefly reviewed.  We compare the difference in storage behavior between Na and Li in their analogous electrodes and summarize the sodium storage mechanisms in the available electrode materials.  This review also includes some new results from our group and our thoughts on developing new materials.  Some perspectives and directions on designing better materials for practical applications are pointed out based on knowledge from the literature and our experience.  Through this extensive literature review, the search for suitable electrode and electrolyte materials for stationary sodium-ion batteries is still challenging.  However, after intensive research efforts, we believe that low-cost, long-life and room-temp. sodium-ion batteries would be promising for applications in large-scale energy storage system in the near future.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpqNKJTie6WmbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liXuxKzYCdXIQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhtFOisrzJ&amp;md5=2e02460553edc21e1ea8b73982ed63bb</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref4'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit4" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201401946"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yuan, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liang, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cao, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ai, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Feng, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, H.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A honeycomb-layered Na3Ni2SbO6: a high-rate and cycle-stable cathode for sodium-ion batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Adv.                         cas_cit4R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">4</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A Honeycomb-Layered Na3Ni2SbO6: A High-Rate and Cycle-Stable Cathode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yuan, Dingding; Liang, Xinmiao; Wu, Lin; Cao, Yuliang; Ai, Xinping; Feng, Jiwen; Yang, Hanxi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>

                        cas_cit5R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">5</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Reversible Sodium Ion Insertion in Single Crystalline Manganese Oxide Nanowires with Long Cycle Life</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Cao, Yu-Liang; Xiao, Li-Fen; Wang, Wei; Choi, Dai-Won; Nie, Zi-Min; Yu, Jianguo; Saraf, Laxmikant V.; Yang, Zhenguo; Liu, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Single, cryst., Na4Mn9O18 nanowires were prepd. through polymer pyrolysis using polyacrylates of Na and Mn as precursors.  The optimized Na4Mn9O18 display high crystallinity and a homogeneous nanowire structure this provides a mech.-stable structure as well as a short diffusion path for Na-ion intercalation and extn.  The Na4Mn9O18 nanowires have a high reversible capacity of 128 mA-h/g at 0.1 C, excellent cycleability (77% capacity retention for 1000 cycles at 0.5 C), and promising rate capability for Na-ion battery applications.  The outstanding performance of the Na4Mn9O18 nanowires makes them a promising candidate to construct a viable and low-cost Na-ion battery system for upcoming power and energy storage systems.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrES3043e-CdrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liXuxKzYCdXIQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3MXntVGrtbg%253D&amp;md5=015afcbec81da24c355d3768c299be72</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref6"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref6'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">6</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit6" data-doi="10.1038/ncomms3858"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yu, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Bai, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xiao, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, Y.                         cas_cit6R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">6</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A zero-strain layered metal oxide as the negative electrode for long-life sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang Yuesheng; Yu Xiqian; Xu Shuyin; Bai Jianming; Xiao Ruijuan; Hu Yong-Sheng; Li Hong; Yang Xiao-Qing; Chen Liquan; Huang Xuejie</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2365</span>
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn"></span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">Room-temperature sodium-ion batteries have shown great promise in large-scale energy storage applications for renewable energy and smart grid because of the abundant sodium resources and low cost.  Although many interesting positive electrode materials with acceptable performance have been proposed, suitable negative electrode materials have not been identified and their development is quite challenging.  Here we introduce a layered material, P2-Na0.66[Li0.22Ti0.78]O2, as the negative electrode, which exhibits only ~0.77% volume change during sodium insertion/extraction.  The zero-strain characteristics ensure a potentially long cycle life.  The electrode material also exhibits an average storage voltage of 0.75 V, a practical usable capacity of ca. 100 mAh g(-1), and an apparent Na(+) diffusion coefficient of 1 × 10(-10) cm(-2) s(-1) as well as the best cyclability for a negative electrode material in a half-cell reported to date.  This contribution demonstrates that P2-Na0.66[Li0.22Ti0.78]O2 is a promising negative electrode material for the development of rechargeable long-life sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcTF-vbNmqlKD2Gmni0r9GoKfW6udTcc2eZT_y-ji3m2Rbntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A280%3ADC%252BC3sbis12gsg%253D%253D&amp;md5=34e8f318873aa7ed3226082d3df04b0f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref7"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref7'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">7</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit7" data-doi="10.1038/nmat3309"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yabuuchi, N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kajiyama, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Iwatate, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Nishikawa, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hitomi, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Okuyama, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Usui, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yamada, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Komaba, S.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">P2-type Nax[Fe1/2Mn1/2]O2 made from earth-abundant elements for rechargeable Na batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nat.                         cas_cit7R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">7</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">P2-type Nax[Fe1/2Mn1/2]O2 made from earth-abundant elements for rechargeable Na batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yabuuchi, Naoaki; Kajiyama, Masataka; Iwatate, Junichi; Nishikawa, Heisuke; Hitomi, Shuji; Okuyama, Ryoichi; Usui, Ryo; Yamada, Yasuhiro; Komaba, Shinichi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2012</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">11</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">512-517</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NMAACR</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1476-1122</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Rechargeable Li batteries have risen to prominence as key devices for green and sustainable energy development.  Mn- and Fe-based cathode materials, such as LiMn2O4 and LiFePO4, are used in large-scale batteries for elec. vehicles.  Mn and Fe are abundant elements in the Earth's crust, but Li is not.  In contrast to Li, Na is an attractive charge carrier from elemental abundance.  Recently, some layered materials, where Na can be electrochem. and reversibly extd./inserted, have been reported.  However, their reversible capacity is typically limited to 100 mA-h/g.  Herein, the authors report a new electrode material, P2-Na2/3[Fe1/2Mn1/2]O2, that delivers 190 mA-h/g of reversible capacity in Na cells with the electrochem. active Fe3+/Fe4+ redox.  These results will contribute to the development of rechargeable batteries from the earth-abundant elements operable at room temp.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoHU9moaXs6J7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgzTxbuK3lM_A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38Xmt1GqtL8%253D&amp;md5=519efcb60bb0a6fd4843546d51921eb7</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref8"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref8'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">8</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit8" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201000061"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kim, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kang, S.-H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Slater, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Rood, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Vaughey, J.                         cas_cit8R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">8</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Enabling sodium batteries using lithium-substituted sodium layered transition metal oxide cathodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kim, Donghan; Kang, Sun-Ho; Slater, Michael; Rood, Shawn; Vaughey, John T.; Karan, Naba; Balasubramanian, Mahalingam; Johnson, Christopher S.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>

                        cas_cit9R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">9</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">β-NaMnO2: A High-Performance Cathode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Billaud, Juliette; Clement, Raphaele J.; Armstrong, A. Robert; Canales-Vazquez, Jesus; Rozier, Patrick; Grey, Clare P.; Bruce, Peter G.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the American Chemical Society</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">136</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">49</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">There is much interest in Na-ion batteries for grid storage because of the lower projected cost compared with Li-ion.  Identifying Earth-abundant, low-cost, and safe materials that can function as intercalation cathodes in Na-ion batteries is an important challenge facing the field.  Here such a material, β-NaMnO2, is investigated with a different structure from that of NaMnO2 polymorphs and other compds. studied extensively in the past.  It exhibits a high capacity (of ca. 190 mA h g-1 at a rate of C/20), along with a good rate capability (142 mA h g-1 at a rate of 2C) and a good capacity retention (100 mA h g-1after 100 Na extn./insertion cycles at a rate of 2C).  Powder XRD, HRTEM, and 23Na NMR studies revealed that this compd. exhibits a complex structure consisting of intergrown regions of α-NaMnO2 and β-NaMnO2 domains.  The collapse of the long-range structure at low Na content is expected to compromise the reversibility of the Na extn. and insertion processes occurring upon charge and discharge of the cathode material, resp.  Yet stable, reproducible, and reversible Na intercalation is obsd.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrfuSEdxm9gsrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgzTxbuK3lM_A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhvFagtr3K&amp;md5=44b446f5da7c455299e8079a0a01fdac</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref10"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref10'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">10</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit10" data-doi="10.1021/nl501152f"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Fang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xiao, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Qian, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ai, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cao, Y.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Mesoporous Amorphous FePO4 Nanospheres as High-Performance Cathode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nano Lett.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2014</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">14</span><span class="NLM_x"> (</span><span class="NLM_issue">6</span><span class="NLM_x">) </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">3539</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">43</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit11R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">11</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Atomic Structure and Kinetics of NASICON NaxV2(PO4)3 Cathode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jian, Zelang; Yuan, Chenchen; Han, Wenze; Lu, Xia; Gu, Lin; Xi, Xuekui; Hu, Yong-Sheng; Li, Hong; Chen, Wen; Chen, Dongfeng; Ikuhara, Yuichi; Chen, Liquan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na3V2(PO4)3 is one of the most important cathode materials for sodium-ion batteries, delivering about two Na extn./insertion from/into the unit structure.  To understand the mechanism of sodium storage, a detailed structure of rhombohedral Na3V2(PO4)3 and its sodium extd. phase of NaV2(PO4)3 are investigated at the at. scale using a variety of advanced techniques.  It is found that two different Na sites (6b, M1 and 18e, M2) with different coordination environments co-exist in Na3V2(PO4)3, whereas only one Na site (6b, M1) exists in NaV2(PO4)3.  When Na is extd. from Na3V2(PO4)3 to form NaV2(PO4)3, Na+ occupying the M2 site (CN = 8) is extd. and the rest of the Na remains at M1 site (CN = 6).  In addn., the Na atoms are not randomly distributed, possibly with an ordered arrangement in M2 sites locally for Na3V2(PO4)3.  Na+ ions at the M1 sites in Na3V2(PO4)3 tend to remain immobilized, suggesting a direct M2-to-M2 conduction pathway.  Only Na occupying the M2 sites can be extd., suggesting about two Na atoms are able to be extd. from the Na3V2(PO4)3 structure.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp-DvM8fZFKKLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljc-WBuEjexZw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXlsFyitrg%253D&amp;md5=a5649ece23092fbf7e2b8ae11cfa73be</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref12"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref12'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">12</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit12" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201502018"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Fang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xiao, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ai, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cao, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, H.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Hierarchical Carbon Framework Wrapped Na3V2(PO4)3 as a Superior High-Rate and Extended Lifespan Cathode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Adv.                         cas_cit13R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">13</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Carbon-Coated Na3V2(PO4)3 Embedded in Porous Carbon Matrix: An Ultrafast Na-Storage Cathode with the Potential of Outperforming Li Cathodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhu, Changbao; Song, Kepeng; van Aken, Peter A.; Maier, Joachim; Yu, Yan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na ion batteries are one of the realistic promising alternatives to the Li analogs.  However, neither theor. energy/power d. nor the practical values reach the values of Li cathodes.  Poorer performance is expected owing to larger size, larger mass, and lower cell voltage.  Nonetheless, Na ion batteries are considered to be practically relevant in view of the abundance of the element Na.  The arguments in favor of Li and to the disadvantage of Na would be completely obsolete if the specific performance data of the latter would match the 1st.  Here the authors present a cathode consisting of C-coated nanosized Na3V2(PO4)3 embedded in a porous C matrix, which not only matches but even out-shines Li cathodes under high rate conditions.  It can be (dis)charged in 6 s with a c.d. ≤22 A/g (200 C), still delivering a specific capacity of 44 mA-h/g, while up to 20 C, the polarization is completely negligible.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpm8FtVi3VfobVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljc-WBuEjexZw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXltF2ksb8%253D&amp;md5=b17dd9cbfe1795da852cd74116af9988</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref14'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit14" data-doi="10.1016/j.elecom.2012.06.014"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Oh, S.-M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Myung, S.-T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hassoun, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Scrosati, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sun, Y.-K.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Reversible NaFePO4 electrode for sodium secondary batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Electrochem.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The behavior of a NaFePO4 cathode, obtained by electrochem. Li-Na exchange of LiFePO4 olivine, is characterized in a sodium battery.  The NaFePO4 electrode here developed shows remarkable electrochem. properties in the sodium cell, such as long charge-discharge cycle life and high rate capability.  X-ray diffraction anal. reveals that the NaFePO4 electrode keeps its original structure upon 50 charge-discharge cycles.  The Na/NaFePO4 battery operates with a working voltage of 2.7 V and a stable capacity of 125 mAh g- 1, namely at 80% of the theor. value.  The results here reported demonstrate that the olivine NaFePO4 electrode is indeed a very promising pos. electrode for the development of high performance, advanced sodium batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrvNCZLzxaJLbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljc-WBuEjexZw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XhtFSru7vE&amp;md5=6b771abfe90a9470452ff9c768c29b0e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref15"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref15'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">15</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit15" data-doi="10.1002/advs.201600392"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Fang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xiao, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ai, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cao, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, H.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Phosphate Framework Electrode Materials for Sodium Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Adv.                         cas_cit15R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">15</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Phosphate Framework Electrode Materials for Sodium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Fang Yongjin; Zhang Jiexin; Ai Xinping; Cao Yuliang; Yang Hanxi; Xiao Lifen</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced science (Weinheim, Baden-Wurttemberg, Germany)</span>

    </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium ion batteries (SIBs) have been considered as a promising alternative for the next generation of electric storage systems due to their similar electrochemistry to Li-ion batteries and the low cost of sodium resources.  Exploring appropriate electrode materials with decent electrochemical performance is the key issue for development of sodium ion batteries.  Due to the high structural stability, facile reaction mechanism and rich structural diversity, phosphate framework materials have attracted increasing attention as promising electrode materials for sodium ion batteries.  Herein, we review the latest advances and progresses in the exploration of phosphate framework materials especially related to single-phosphates, pyrophosphates and mixed-phosphates.  We provide the detailed and comprehensive understanding of structure-composition-performance relationship of materials and try to show the advantages and disadvantages of the materials for use in SIBs.  In addition, some new perspectives about phosphate framework materials for SIBs are also discussed.  Phosphate framework materials will be a competitive and attractive choice for use as electrodes in the next-generation of energy storage devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcTMcbcHlPuAMBwLZxei1HN8fW6udTcc2ea9eEcALmEhQrntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A280%3ADC%252BC1cnhsFehsQ%253D%253D&amp;md5=5afdb3cd74a61df70f70c83d0ead6440</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref16"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref16'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">16</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit16" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201100655"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Qian, J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium manganese hexacyanoferrate cathode materials with two structures can be synthesized at room temp.  The sodium-ion concn. in the aq. soln. during pptn. has a strong influence on the compn. and structure of the final product, resulting in different reversible capacity and cycling performance.  With higher Na+ concn., a cooperative Na+ displacement along a single [111] direction induces a transition from cubic to rhombohedral symmetry - this phase transition is reversible on cycling the Na+ concn.                         "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref19"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref19'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">19</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit19" data-doi="10.1039/c4ta00106k"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Duan, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cheng, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Na3V2(PO4)3@C core-shell nanocomposites for rechargeable sodium-ion batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J. Mater. Chem. A</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2014</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">2</span><span class="NLM_x"> (</span><span class="NLM_issue">23</span><span class="NLM_x">) </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">8668</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">8675</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit19R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">19</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Na3V2(PO4)3@C core-shell nanocomposites for rechargeable sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Duan, Wenchao; Zhu, Zhiqiang; Li, Hao; Hu, Zhe; Zhang, Kai; Cheng, Fangyi; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">2</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">23</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">8668-8675</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na3V2(PO4)3 (NVP) is an attractive cathode material for sodium ion batteries due to its high theor. energy d. and stable three-dimensional (3D) NASICON structure.  A NVP@C core-shell nanocomposite was synthesized through a hydrothermal assisted sol-gel method.  Ascorbic acid and polyethylene glycol 400 (PEG-400) were synergistically used to control the particle growth and provide the surface coating of conductive carbon.  The as-prepd. nanocomposite was composed of a nanosized Na3V2(PO4)3 core with a typical size of ∼40 nm and a uniformly amorphous carbon shell with the thickness of a few nanometers.  The electrode performance of the NVP@C core-shell nanocomposite as cathode for sodium ion batteries is studied and compared with that of bare NVP and NVP/C.  Among the samples examd., the NVP@C nanocomposite showed the best cycle life and rate capability.  It rendered an initial capacity of 104.3 mA h g-1 at 0.5 C and 94.9 mA h g-1 at 5 C with a remarkable capacity retention of 96.1% after 700 cycles.  Also, a full cell using the as-prepd. nanocomposite as both the cathode and the anode active material was successfully built, showing a reversible capacity of 90.9 mA h g-1 at 2 C with an output voltage of ∼1.7 V and a specific energy d. of ∼154.5 W h kg-1.  The enhanced electrode performance is attributed to the combination of particle downsizing and carbon coating, which can favor the migration of both electrons and ions.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo-MXnruCyFELVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li_wFXCqrwVcA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXosVWqtLw%253D&amp;md5=d86081db0910b2756c626f1f1abf470d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref20"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref20'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">20</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit20" data-doi="10.1016/j.elecom.2011.11.009"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jian, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhao, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Pan, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, Y.-S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, L.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Carbon coated Na3V2(PO4)3 as novel electrode material for sodium ion batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Electrochem. Commun.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2012</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">14</span><span class="NLM_x"> (</span><span class="NLM_issue">1</span><span class="NLM_x">) </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">86</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">89</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.elecom.2011.11.009</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D14%26publication_year%3D2012%26pages%3D86-89%26journal%3DElectrochem.%2BCommun.%26issue%3D1%26author%3DZ.%2BJian%26author%3DL.%2BZhao%26author%3DH.%2BPan%26author%3DY.-S.%2BHu%26author%3DH.%2BLi%26author%3DW.%2BChen%26author%3DL.%2BChen%26title%3DCarbon%2Bcoated%2BNa3V2%2528PO4%25293%2Bas%2Bnovel%2Belectrode%2Bmaterial%2Bfor%2Bsodium%2Bion%2Bbatteries%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.elecom.2011.11.009&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.6b16000&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.elecom.2011.11.009&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit20R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">20</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Carbon coated Na3V2(PO4)3 as novel electrode material for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jian, Zelang; Zhao, Liang; Pan, Huilin; Hu, Yong-Sheng; Li, Hong; Chen, Wen; Chen, Liquan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochemistry Communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2012</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">14</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">86-89</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ECCMF9</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1388-2481</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A Na3V2(PO4)3 sample coated uniformly with a layer of 6 nm carbon has been successfully synthesized by a one-step solid state reaction.  This material shows two flat voltage plateaus at 3.4 V vs. Na+/Na and 1.63 V vs. Na+/Na in a nonaq. sodium cell.  When the Na3V2(PO4)3/C sample is tested as a cathode in a voltage range of 2.7-3.8 V vs. Na+/Na, its initial charge and discharge capacities are 98.6 and 93 mAh/g.  The capacity retention of 99% can be achieved after 10 cycles.  The electrode shows good cycle performance and moderate rate performance.  When it is tested as an anode in a voltage range of 1.0-3.0 V vs.  Na+/Na, the initial reversible capacity is 66.3 mAh/g and the capacity of 59 mAh/g can be maintained after 50 cycles.  These preliminary results indicate that Na3V2(PO4)3/C is a new promising material for sodium ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrBLuN7XBpzrrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li_wFXCqrwVcA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3MXhs1SlsrnK&amp;md5=e12fcddddd82fd72385af411bb5d72f8</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref21"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref21'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">21</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit21" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2014.09.153"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Bai, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, C.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Budding willow branches shaped Na3V2(PO4)3/C nanofibers synthesized via an electrospinning technique and used as cathode material for sodium ion batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J. Power Sources</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">273</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">784</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">792</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.jpowsour.2014.09.153</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D273%26publication_year%3D2015%26pages%3D784-792%26journal%3DJ.%2BPower%2BSources%26author%3DH.%2BLi%26author%3DY.%2BBai%26author%3DF.%2BWu%26author%3DY.%2BLi%26author%3DC.%2BWu%26title%3DBudding%2Bwillow%2Bbranches%2Bshaped%2BNa3V2%2528PO4%25293%252FC%2Bnanofibers%2Bsynthesized%2Bvia%2Ban%2Belectrospinning%2Btechnique%2Band%2Bused%2Bas%2Bcathode%2Bmaterial%2Bfor%2Bsodium%2Bion%2Bbatteries%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.jpowsour.2014.09.153&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.6b16000&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.jpowsour.2014.09.153&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Budding willow branches shaped Na3V2(PO4)3/C nanofibers synthesized via an electrospinning technique and used as cathode material for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Hui; Bai, Ying; Wu, Feng; Li, Yu; Wu, Chuan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">273</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">784-792</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPSODZ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0378-7753</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Budding willow branches shaped Na3V2(PO4)3/C nanofibers were successfully synthesized by a simple electrospinning technique with Poly(vinyl pyrrilidone) (PVP).  The Na3V2(PO4)3/C nanoparticles that anchored on the nanofibers surface seemed like the willow buds; the inner core of the nanofibers, which composed Na3V2(PO4)3, looked like willow twig and the uniform carbon layer was same with willow bark.  Such special morphol. played a vital role in improving cycle stability and rate capability of the electrode due to the conductive network built up by nanofibers.  The Na3V2(PO4)3/C nanofibers cathode exhibited an initial specific capacity of 106.8 mAh g-1 at a c.d. of 0.2C, still stabling at 107.2 mAh g-1 after 125 cycles with excellent cycle stability.  Moreover, a capacity retention of 95.7% was obtained when Na3V2(PO4)3/C nanofibers cycled stepwise from 0.2 to 2C.  Good electrochem. performance should be ascribed to both the special morphol. and preferential growth of the (113) plane.  The simple synthesis technique and good electrochem. performance suggests that this material with the special shape of budding willow branches is a promising cathode for sodium ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrVz97DbrTI97Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljF3GJckFyfZg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhslajt7jO&amp;md5=69963f6a9036aa0fd36127b2385b57ae</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref22'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit22" data-doi="10.1039/c3ta12116j"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jung, Y. H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lim, C. H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kim, D. K.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Graphene-supported Na3V2(PO4)3 as a high rate cathode material for sodium-ion batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J. Mater. A</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2013</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">1</span><span class="NLM_x"> (</span><span class="NLM_issue">37</span><span class="NLM_x">) </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">11350</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/c3ta12116j</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D1%26publication_year%3D2013%26pages%3D11350%26journal%3DJ.%2BMater.%2BChem.%2BA%26issue%3D37%26author%3DY.%2BH.%2BJung%26author%3DC.%2BH.%2BLim%26author%3DD.%2BK.%2BKim%26title%3DGraphene-supported%2BNa3V2%2528PO4%25293%2Bas%2Ba%2Bhigh%2Brate%2Bcathode%2Bmaterial%2Bfor%2Bsodium-ion%2Bbatteries%26doi%3D10.1039%252Fc3ta12116j&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.6b16000&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2Fc3ta12116j&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit22R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">22</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Graphene-supported Na3V2(PO4)3 as a high rate cathode material for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jung, Young Hwa; Lim, Chek Hai; Kim, Do Kyung</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">1</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">37</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">11350-11354</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Substantial interest in Na resources that are inexpensive and abundant in the earth has guided intense research on Na-based electrode materials.  The authors report a facile synthetic strategy to improve the rate performance of Na-based electrode materials in Na-ion batteries.  Na3V2(PO4)3 (NVP) is one of the most promising cathode materials with a NASICON structure, and it was synthesized on a graphene sheet surface using a simple method that combines sol-gel and solid-state reaction.  The NVP/graphene composite displays an excellent high-rate performance; it delivers ∼67% of the initial 0.2 C capacity at a 30 C rate, whereas bare NVP produces only 46% of the 0.2 C capacity at a 5 C rate.  It also demonstrates high capacity retention both at 1 C and 10 C cycles as a promising cathode for rechargeable Na-ion batteries.  This outstanding result can be ascribed to the key role of graphene in enhancing the electronic cond. of electrode materials compared with bare NVP.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrgIo_IQIvvY7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljF3GJckFyfZg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhtlClsbzM&amp;md5=327c052bc9b25fafc2ce5af15b955571</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref23"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref23'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">23</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit23" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201402104"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jiang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zeng, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Pan, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wei, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, G.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Gu, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yu, Y.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Nanoconfined Carbon-Coated Na3V2(PO4)3 Particles in Mesoporous Carbon Enabling Ultralong Cycle Life for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Adv.                         cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High rate performance of a Na3V2(PO4)3/C cathode prepared by pyro-synthesis for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kang, Jungwon; Baek, Sora; Mathew, Vinod; Gim, Jihyeon; Song, Jinju; Park, Hyosun; Chae, Eunji; Rai, Alok Kumar; Kim, Jaekook</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry</span>

                        cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Na3V2(PO4)3 particles partly embedded in carbon nanofibers with superb kinetics for ultra-high power sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yang, Junghoon; Han, Dong-Wook; Jo, Mi Ru; Song, Kyeongse; Kim, Yong-Il; Chou, Shu-Lei; Liu, Hua-Kun; Kang, Yong-Mook</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1005-1009</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">We here describe the extraordinary performance of NASICON Na3V2(PO4)3-carbon nanofiber (NVP-CNF) composites with ultra-high power and excellent cycling performance.  NVP-CNFs are composed of CNFs at the center part and partly embedded NVP nanoparticles in the shell.  We first report this unique morphol. of NVP-CNFs for the electrode material of secondary batteries as well as for general energy conversion materials.  Our NVP-CNFs show not only a high discharge capacity of ∼88.9 mA h g-1 even at a high c.d. of 50 C but also ∼93% cyclic retention property after 300 cycles at 1 C.  The superb kinetics and excellent cycling performance of the NVP-CNFs are attributed to the facile migration of Na ions through the partly exposed regions of NVP nanoparticles that are directly in contact with an electrolyte as well as the fast electron transfer along the conducting CNF pathways.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrsUWuYo75Bq7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljF3GJckFyfZg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhvF2ksLzF&amp;md5=5696d6f6e7feeefb1f86d354921572d8</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit28" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201305522"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Dong, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">He, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Mai, L.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Effect of carbon matrix dimensions on the electrochemical properties of Na3V2(PO4)3 nanograins for high-performance symmetric sodium-ion batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Adv.                         cas_cit28R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">28</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Effect of Carbon Matrix Dimensions on the Electrochemical Properties of Na3V2(PO4)3 Nanograins for High-Performance Symmetric Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Shuo; Dong, Yifan; Xu, Lin; Xu, Xu; He, Liang; Mai, Liqiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The electrochem. properties of Na3V2(PO4)3 nanograins having different carbon contents were investigated by a one-step solid state reaction and evaluated in different electrolyte systems.  It was found that the sodium storage performance in terms of capacity, coulombic efficiency and cyclability can be significantly improved in a new sodium bis(fluorosulfonyl) imide/propylene carbonate electrolyte which is introduced for the first time, bringing this material close to viability as a promising cathode for room-temp. sodium-ion batteries.  The mechanism of sodium insertion/extn. into/from Na3V2(PO4)3 lattice is analyzed by in-situ XRD technique.         ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0013-4651</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Electrochemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A combined exptl. and computational study on Na3V2(PO4)3 was carried out to study its structural, electrochem. and thermal properties as a Na battery cathode.  The synthesized material by a sol-gel process was well-indexed to the R-3m space group in the framework of a rhombohedral NASICON structure.  Galvanostatic measurements indicate that at 3.4 V vs. Na/Na+, 1.4 Na reversibly reacts with each Na3V2(PO4)3, which corresponds to a specific capacity of 84.8 mA-h/g.  Also, this material shows excellent rate capabilities and good cycling performance.  Ex-situ XRD analyzes indicate that this material reacts with Na ions based on a reversible 2-phase reaction.  Thermal analyzes employing TGA/DSC and In-situ XRD at various temps. show that this material maintains good thermal stability up to 450° even in the de-sodiated state.  The electrochem. and thermal properties suggest that this material with the well-defined NASICON structure is a promising cathode for large-scale Na rechargeable batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo403l0EIXW1rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liGwgjVzjbutQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XhsVylurzF&amp;md5=a8c95bf4b6c24af2c8d2908c2d791ef3</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref30'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit30" data-doi="10.1039/C5TA01007A"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Mao, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Luo, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Gao, T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Fan, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, C.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Scalable synthesis of Na3V2(PO4)3/C porous hollow spheres as a cathode for Na-ion batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J. Mater. Chem. A</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">3</span><span class="NLM_x"> (</span><span class="NLM_issue">19</span><span class="NLM_x">) </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">10378</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">10385</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit30R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">30</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Scalable synthesis of Na3V2(PO4)3/C porous hollow spheres as a cathode for Na-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Mao, Jianfeng; Luo, Chao; Gao, Tao; Fan, Xiulin; Wang, Chunsheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">19</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">10378-10385</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na3V2(PO4)3 has been considered as a very promising cathode material for sodium-ion batteries due to its typical NASICON structure, which provides an open and three-dimensional framework for Na+ migration.  However, the low electronic cond. of Na3V2(PO4)3 limits its rate capability and cycling ability.  In this study, carbon coated hollow structured Na3V2(PO4)3/C composites are synthesized via a template-free and scalable ultrasonic spray pyrolysis process, where the carbon coated Na3V2(PO4)3 particles are uniformly decorated on the inner and outer surfaces of the porous hollow carbon spheres.  When evaluated as a cathode material for sodium-ion batteries, the unique Na3V2(PO4)3/C porous hollow sphere cathode delivers an initial discharge capacity of 99.2 mA-h/g and retains 89.3 mA-h/g after 300 charge/discharge cycles with a very low degrdn. rate of 0.035% per cycle.  For comparison, the Na3V2(PO4)3/C composite, prepd. by the traditional sol-gel method, delivers a lower initial discharge capacity of 97.4 mA-h/g and decreases significantly to 71.5 mA-h/g after 300 cycles.  The superior electrochem. performance of Na3V2(PO4)3/C porous hollow spheres is attributed to their unique porous, hollow and spherical structures, as well as the carbon coating layer, which provides a high contact area between electrode/electrolyte, high electronic cond., and high mech. strength.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoFJehH2JWLd7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liGwgjVzjbutQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXmtF2qtbg%253D&amp;md5=8d96b668c4e447e1dd8e5ffe7ebaf3cf</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref31"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref31'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">31</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit31" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201200803"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Saravanan, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Mason, C. W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Rudola, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wong, K. H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Balaya, P.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">The First Report on Excellent Cycling Stability and Superior Rate Capability of Na3V2(PO4)3for Sodium Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Adv.                         cas_cit31R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">31</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">The first report on excellent cycling stability and superior rate capability of Na3V2(PO4)3 for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Saravanan, Kuppan; Mason, Chad W.; Rudola, Ashish; Wong, Kim Hai; Balaya, Palani</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">444-450</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADEMBC</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-Blackwell</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium ion batteries are attractive for the rapidly emerging large-scale energy storage market for intermittent renewable resources.  Currently a viable cathode material does not exist for practical non-aq. sodium ion battery applications.  Here we disclose a high performance, durable electrode material based on the 3D NASICON framework.  Porous Na3V2(PO4)3/C was synthesized using a novel soln.-based approach.  This material, as a cathode, is capable of delivering an energy storage capacity of ∼400 mWh/g vs. sodium metal.  Furthermore, at high current rates (10, 20 and 40 C), it displayed remarkable capacity retention.  Equally impressive is the long term cycle life.  Nearly 50% of the initial capacity was retained after 30,000 charge/discharge cycles at 40 C (4.7 A/g).  Notably, coulombic efficiency was 99.68% (av.) over the course of cycling.  To the best of our knowledge, the combination of high energy d., high power d. and ultra long cycle life demonstrated here has never been reported before for sodium ion batteries.  We believe our findings will have profound implications for developing large-scale energy storage systems for renewable energy sources.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqDJwVCxsh14rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liGwgjVzjbutQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXmtFaks7Y%253D&amp;md5=de231bc6c1bc62101fab4472580ebdfa</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit32" data-doi="10.1002/smll.201500783"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Huang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, X.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Flexible and Binder-Free Electrodes of Sb/rGO and Na3V2(PO4)3/rGO Nanocomposites for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Small</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">11</span><span class="NLM_x"> (</span><span class="NLM_issue">31</span><span class="NLM_x">) </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">3822</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">3829</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Flexible and Binder-Free Electrodes of Sb/rGO and Na3V2(PO4)3/rGO Nanocomposites for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Wei; Liu, Yangtao; Chen, Chaoji; Li, Zhen; Huang, Yunhui; Hu, Xianluo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">11</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">31</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3822-3829</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">SMALBC</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Flexible power sources showed great promise in next-generation bendable, implantable, and wearable electronic systems.  Here, flexible and binder-free electrodes of Na3V2(PO4)3/reduced graphene oxide (NVP/rGO) and Sb/rGO nanocomposites for Na-ion batteries are reported.  The Sb/rGO and NVP/rGO paper electrodes with high flexibility and tailorability can be easily fabricated.  Sb and NVP nanoparticles are embedded homogeneously in the interconnected framework of rGO nanosheets, which provides structurally stable hosts for Na-ion intercalation and deintercalation.  The NVP/rGO paper-like cathode delivers a reversible capacity of 113 mA h g-1 at 100 mA g-1 and high capacity retention of ≈96.6% after 120 cycles.  The Sb/rGO paper-like anode gives a highly reversible capacity of 612 mA h g-1 at 100 mA g-1, an excellent rate capacity up to 30 C, and a good cycle performance.  Also, the Na-ion full cell of NVP/rGO//Sb/rGO was fabricated, delivering a highly reversible capacity of ≈400 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 100 mA g-1 after 100 charge/discharge cycles.  This work may provide promising electrode candidates for developing next-generation energy-storage devices with high capacity and long cycle life.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqEuCL3VQtFtbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liGwgjVzjbutQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXnsFCltrw%253D&amp;md5=c6e885e922194d560b18ff20c7794ae7</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref33'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit33" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201502864"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Rui, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sun, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yan, Q.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">An Advanced Sodium-Ion Battery Composed of Carbon Coated Na3V2(PO4)3 in a Porous Graphene Network</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Adv.                         cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">An Advanced Sodium-Ion Battery Composed of Carbon Coated Na3V2(PO4)3 in a Porous Graphene Network</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Rui, Xianhong; Sun, Wenping; Wu, Chao; Yu, Yan; Yan, Qingyu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">27</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">6670-6676</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Herein, to create efficient charge transfer, we propose a 3D hierarchical meso- and macroporous NVP-based hybrid cathode concept with connected Na ion/electron pathways for ultrafast charge and discharge NIBs, consisting of NVP nanocrystals coated with amorphous carbon and then wrapped by reduced graphene oxide nanosheets (abbreviated as NVP@C@rGO).  Specifically, i) the small nanograins shorten the lengths of solid-state Na ion diffusion, ii) the macro/mesopore network enables rapid ion transport and buffers the strain during repeated Na+ extn./insertion to maintain the structural integrity, iii) highly conductive amorphous coating carbon and rGO nanosheets facilitate fast electron transfer within the electrode and to the current collector.  The designed NVP@C@rGO cathode is shown to achieve excellent rate capability (86 mA h/g at 100 C) and outstandingcycling stability (64% retention after 10000 cycles at 100 C), indicating its superiority in practical applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqsi-wIi2kQlbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liGwgjVzjbutQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsF2ksrrM&amp;md5=7861bc14c4a3396b8223e56a8e698e3b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref34'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit34" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201502197"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Fang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xiao, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Qian, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cao, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ai, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Huang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, H.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">3D Graphene Decorated NaTi2(PO4)(3) Microspheres as a Superior High-Rate and Ultracycle-Stable Anode Material for Sodium Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Adv.                         cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Fabrication of graphene-encapsulated Na3V2(PO4)3 as high-performance cathode materials for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Tao, Shi; Wang, Xingbo; Cui, Peixin; Wang, Yu; Haleem, Yasir A.; Wei, Shenghui; Huang, Weifeng; Song, Li; Chu, Wangsheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">RSC Advances</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">49</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">43591-43597</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">RSCACL</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2046-2069</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na3V2(PO4)3 (NVP) has been in the spotlight as a potential candidate of next generation batteries to overcome the limitation of lithium resources on Earth.  Here a thin-layer graphene-encapsulated NVP composite (NVP/G) was synthesized by self-assembly of surface modified NVP and graphene oxide and then followed by redn. to compensate for the intrinsic low electronic cond. of NVP and strengthen its structure stability.  The as-synthesized hybrid composite as a cathode for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) exhibits excellent high specific capacity and superior rate performance with discharge capacities of 115.2 mA h g-1 at 0.2 C and 70.1 mA h g-1 at 30 C, It also shows an excellent cycling stability with about 86.0% capacity retention at 5 C after 300 cycles.  Ex situ X-ray absorption spectroscopy (XAS) characterization confirmes the local geometrical environment around vanadium is highly conserved during the sodiation/desodiation process, assocd. with an electrochem. active V3+/V4+ redox couple.  Hence the as-prepd. hybrid composite can be considered as a promising cathode material for high-rate SIBs, thanks to the effect interface interaction between NVP nanoparticle sand graphene films.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqhpntxy9HNybVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgQKH4zgA0Daw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XmslKnu7g%253D&amp;md5=0499ac95efa524dec45d387dd03df83b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref38'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit38" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201600389"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wei, Q.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, Q.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">An, Q.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sheng, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Mai, L.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Layer-by-Layer Na3V2(PO4)3Embedded in Reduced Graphene Oxide as Superior Rate and Ultralong-Life Sodium-Ion Battery Cathode</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Adv. Energy Mater.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2013</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">3</span><span class="NLM_x"> (</span><span class="NLM_issue">2</span><span class="NLM_x">) </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">156</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">160</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit40R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">40</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Superior electrochemical performance and storage mechanism of Na3V2(PO4)3 cathode for room-temperature sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jian, Zelang; Han, Wenze; Lu, Xia; Yang, Huaixin; Hu, Yong-Sheng; Zhou, Jing; Zhou, Zhibin; Li, Jianqi; Chen, Wen; Chen, Dongfeng; Chen, Liquan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">156-160</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADEMBC</span>;

        </div><div class="casAbstract">In this article, Na3V2(PO4)3/carbon nanocomposites with different carbon contents were prepd. by a one-step solid state reaction and evaluated in different electrolyte systems.  It was found that the sodium storage performance in terms of capacity, coulombic efficiency and cyclability can be significantly improved in a new sodium bis(fluorosulfonyl) imide/propylene carbonate electrolyte which is introduced for the first time, bringing this material close to viability as a promising cathode for room-temp. sodium-ion batteries.                         cas_cit41R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">41</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Na3V2(PO4)3/C composite as the intercalation-type anode material for sodium-ion batteries with superior rate capability and long-cycle life</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Dongxue; Chen, Nan; Li, Malin; Wang, Chunzhong; Ehrenberg, Helmut; Bie, Xiaofei; Wei, Yingjin; Chen, Gang; Du, Fei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">16</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">8636-8642</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
